Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
12 min
Reconciling Hadiths on Basmalah and Hamd: Ibtida Types and Evidence
Resolving apparent contradiction via ibtida types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the three types of ibtida (haqiqi, idafi, urfi) to reconcile apparently conflicting hadiths and identify the Quranic and ijma evidence supporting the Hanafi position on basmalah precedence.

Core Idea
Two conflicting hadiths can both be valid by interpreting 'beginning' as absolute in one and relative or customary in the other.

When two hadiths seem to contradict, the Hanafi method first attempts reconciliation (jam') over preference (tarjih). This passage resolves the apparent conflict between the hadiths commanding basmalah and hamd by introducing three meanings of 'ibtida' (beginning). The author also provides Quranic and consensus evidence for the precedence of basmalah. Understanding this method is crucial for usul al-fiqh students to handle textual conflicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting hadiths
Recognize that there are two hadiths: 'Kullu amrin dhi balin la yubda'u fihi bi-bismillah…' and 'Kullu amrin dhi balin la yubda'u fihi bi-hamdillah…'. They appear to command different things to begin with.
These hadiths are well-known in fiqh literature.
2
Understand the problem and solution framework
The literal contradiction arises because only one thing can be truly first. The solution is to distinguish different types of 'beginning'.
The Hanafi principle: jam' is preferred over tarjih when possible.
3
Learn the three types of ibtida
Study the definitions: (1) Haqiqi – absolute precedence over everything; (2) Idafi – relative precedence over some and posterior to others; (3) Urfi – customary precedence in people's opinion.
These allow flexibility in applying the term 'beginning'.
4
Apply the classification to the hadiths
Assign haqiqi ibtida to the basmalah hadith, and idafi or urfi ibtida to the hamd hadith. This way, basmalah is truly first, but hamd is still first in a relative or customary sense, removing the contradiction.
Thus both hadiths are implemented.
5
Review the supporting evidence
The author cites Quran 27:30 (Basmalah in Sulayman's letter) and the practical consensus (ijma) of the ummah on giving precedence to basmalah. This strengthens the Hanafi position.
The objection about Sulayman placing his own name first is answered by the wisdom of protecting Allah's name from potential insult.

ترجمہ! مگر مقدم کیا مصنف نے تسمیہ کو اس لئے کہ دونوں نھیں ظاہر ا آپس میں متعارض تھیں اسلئے کہ ابتداء دو چیزوں میں سے ایک کیساتھ فوت کر دیتی ہے ابتداء کو دوسری چیز کیساتھ اور ممکن ہے جمع کرنا بایں طور کہ مقدم کی جائے اُن میں سے ایک دوسری پریس قومہ بہائے اس کیساتھ ابتداء حقیقی اور دوسری کے ساتھ نسبت کرتے ہوئے اس کے ماسوا کی طرف پس مصنف نے کتاب اللہ کے ساتھ عمل کیا جو وارد ہوئی ہے تسمیہ کو مقدم کرنے کے ساتھ اور اجماع کے ساتھ جو منعقد ہوا ہے تقدیم تسمیہ پر ۔ غرض جواب سوال مقدر سوال ! مصنف کی یہ کوشش وسعی لاحاصل ہے اگر چہ دونوں کو قید بنا کر دونوں میں تسویہ اختیار کیا گیا لیکن دونوں حدیثین پر عمل ناممکن ہے اگر تسمیہ کو اولا حال بنا کر ذکر کیا گیا تو ابتداء صرف تسمیہ کے ساتھ ہوگی اگر تحمید کو اولا ذکر کیا یہ ہے تو ابتداء بالتسمیہ نہیں ہوگی تو ایک حدیث ضرور متروک ہوگی کیونکہ معنی ابتداء اول کل شی ء ہے اور وہ صر ف ایک سے ہو سکتی ہے یا تسمیہ سے یا تحمید ہے۔ جواب ! ( تمہید ) ابتداء کی تین اقسام ہیں (۱) حقیقی ما ھو مقدم علی الکل (۲) اضافي ما هو مقدم على البعض ومؤخر عن البعض (۳) ابتداء عرفی ما ھو مقدم عن المقصود ۔ جواب ! حاصل جواب یہ ہے کہ اشکال مذکور تب لازم آتا ہے جب دونوں حدیثوں میں ابتداء سے ابتداء حقیقی مراد لی جائے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں پبلکہ حدیث تسمیہ میں ابتداء حقیقی اور حدیث تحمید میں ابتداء اضافی مراد ہے۔ جواب ! (۲) حدیث تسمیہ سے ابتداء حقیقی حدیث تحمید سے ابتداء عرفی مراد ہے۔ جواب ! (۳) دونوں سے ابتداء عرفی مراد ہے اس صورت میں دونوں حدیثوں پر عمل ہوگا کوئی متروک نہ ہوگی ۔ فعمل با الكتاب غرض جواب سوال مقدر ۔ سوال ! یہ ہے کہ حدیث تسمیہ کو ابتداء حقیقی پر محمول کر کے تسمیہ کو مقدم کیوں کیا حدیث تحمید کو ابتداء حقیقی پر کیوں محمول نہ کیا۔ جواب! (۱) اقتداء بکتاب اللہ عز وجل کیونکہ کتاب اللہ میں تسمیہ کو حمید پر مقدم کیا گیا (۲) امت کا اجماع عملی ہے تقدیم تسمیہ علی الحمید پر عمل بالا جماع جواب (۳) خط سلیمان الی بلقیس پر عمل کرتے ہوئے وانہ بسم اللہ الرحمان الرحیم ۔ سوال ! سلیمان علیہ السلام نے خط میں اپنے نام کو اسم اللہ پر مقدم کیا حالانکہ اس میں سوء ادب ہے؟ جواب ! تقدیم میں حکمت یہ تھی کہ عموما غیر مذہب و اہل باطل کو کوئی تحریر دی جائے تو وہ نام دیکھ کر سب وشتم و بے ادبی کا مظاہرہ کرتے ہیں تو اپنا نام اول تحریر کیا تا کہ میرے نام کی تو ہین ہو نہ کہ اللہ تعالی کی۔
It is possible to reconcile by giving precedence to one of them over the other, so the beginning occurs with that one in reality, and with the other in relation to what is other than it. So he acted according to the Book which came with giving precedence to tasmiah, and the consensus held upon it. Translation: The author gave precedence to tasmiah because the two hadiths are apparently conflicting, since beginning with one thing eliminates beginning with the other. It is possible to reconcile by giving precedence to one of them over the other, so that the beginning with it is haqiqi and with the other is idafi. So the author acted according to the Book of Allah which came with giving precedence to tasmiah, and the consensus held on precedence of tasmiah. In short, answer to the supposed question: The author's effort is pointless... Answer: (Preamble) Ibtida has three types: (1) Haqiqi: what is prior to everything; (2) Idafi: what is prior to some and posterior to some; (3) Urfi: what is prior in the opinion. Answer: The crux is that the objection applies only if ibtida in both hadiths is taken as haqiqi, but it is not so. Rather, in the hadith of tasmiah, ibtida is haqiqi, and in the hadith of tahmid, ibtida is idafi. Answer: (2) In the hadith of tasmiah, ibtida is haqiqi; in the hadith of tahmid, ibtida is urfi. Answer: (3) Both are taken as urfi; in that case, both hadiths are acted upon. Then he acted with the Book. Question: Why is tasmiah interpreted as haqiqi and given precedence, while tahmid is not? Answers: (1) Following the Book of Allah, in which tasmiah is given precedence over tahmid; (2) The ummah's practical consensus on giving precedence to tasmiah; (3) Following the letter of Sulayman to Bilqis: 'Innahu min Sulayman wa innahu bismillah al-rahman al-rahim.' Question: Sulayman gave precedence to his own name over Allah's name; is that not disrespect? Answer: The wisdom was that when writing to non-believers, they might insult the name, so he put his name first to protect Allah's name.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage addresses how to reconcile two seemingly contradictory hadiths: 'Kullu amrin dhi balin la yubda'u fihi bi-bismillah…' and 'Kullu amrin dhi balin la yubda'u fihi bi-hamdillah…'. The author explains that the apparent conflict is resolved by understanding that ibtida (beginning) can be haqiqi (absolute precedence), idafi (relative precedence), or urfi (customary precedence). The hadith of tasmiah is taken as haqiqi ibtida, while the hadith of tahmid is taken as idafi or urfi ibtida. Thus both hadiths are acted upon. The author also provides additional evidence from the Quran (Basmalah in Surah al-Naml, 27:30) and the practice of the Prophet Sulayman. This is a classic Hanafi usul methodology of jam' (reconciliation) over tarjih (preference) whenever possible.

Key Terms
الابتداء (al-ibtida): The beginning of an action, divided into haqiqi (absolute precedence), idafi (relative), and urfi (customary).
التسمية (al-tasmiah): Saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'; the act of beginning with basmalah.
التحميد (al-tahmid): Saying 'Alhamdulillah'; the act of praising Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the Hanafi method reconcile the two hadiths on basmalah and hamd?
A) By declaring one hadith abrogated
B) By interpreting ibtida as haqiqi in the basmalah hadith and idafi/urfi in the hamd hadith
C) By rejecting the chain of the hamd hadith
D) By applying the principle of istihsan

Key Takeaway
Two seemingly conflicting hadiths can be reconciled by interpreting key terms like 'ibtida' in different senses, a core Hanafi usul principle.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Hanafi Position on Mutashabihat and Their Purpose
Dispute on interpretation of mutashabihat and their purpose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on who knows the meaning of mutashabihat and explain the purpose of their revelation as a test for the deeply learned.

Core Idea
Only Allah knows the meaning of mutashabihat; their revelation tests the deeply learned.

This passage tackles a foundational usul dispute: who knows the true meaning of the mutashabihat (ambiguous) verses of the Qur'an? The Hanafis hold that only Allah knows, while the Shafi'is include the firmly grounded in knowledge. The passage also addresses the apparent problem that such ambiguous verses seem useless for guidance, and explains that their real benefit is as a trial for scholars. This lesson will help you understand the Hanafi argument and the theological purpose behind ambiguous verses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue of dispute
Recognize that the primary disagreement is about the interpretation of Qur'an 3:7: who knows the ta'wil (interpretation) of the mutashabihat?
The dispute hinges on where to stop (waqf) in the verse.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafis say: stop at 'illa Allah', making 'al-rasikhun' the subject of a new sentence. Thus only Allah knows the ta'wil.
This is based on the grammatical rule of waqf.
3
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
The Shafi'is say: conjoin 'al-rasikhun' to 'Allah', so both know. Stop at 'al-rasikhun'.
They read the verse as 'illa Allah wa al-rasikhun fi al-ilm'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the implied question
The passage answers the objection: if mutashabihat are unknown, why were they revealed? The benefit is a test for scholars, who love knowledge and are prevented from interpreting them.
This shows that the revelation is not futile.
5
Evaluate the commentator's neutrality
Note that Taftazani concealed his own madhhab in his wording, which indicates scholarly adab.
This reflects the principle of avoiding bias in sharh.

Source Text

مسک الملیح والتلويه چیز کو جو کہ وہ نہیں ہے یعنی علم اور طلب میں کوشش کرنا اسی طرح علماء امتحان لئے جاتے ہیں ٹھرنے اور چھوڑ نے کیسا ل و :besturdubooks کے نزدیک محبوب ہے اسلئے کہ ہر آدمی کا امتحان اسکی خواہش کے خلاف اور اسکی تمنا کے برعکس ہوتا ہے۔ قوله مقصورات ای محبوسات سے شارخ نے مقصورات کا معنی بیان کیا۔ جعل خيام الاستتار الخ غرض شارح توضیح متن ہے حاصل یہ ہے کہ مصنف نے آیات متشابہات کو ان اشیاء مستورہ و محبوسہ کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی جن پر بناء واستار کے خیمے لگا دیے گئے ہوں اور وہ جیسے اس طرح ان کو محیط ہوں کہ ان کے ظہور کی امید نہ ہو۔ احناف کا مذہب بھی یہی ہے کہ متشابہات کا معنی مراد خداوند قدوس کے علاوہ کوئی نہیں جانتا اور قرآن پاک میں دم یعلم تاویلہ الا اللہ پر وقف لازم ہے والراسخون فی العلم جملہ علیحدہ ہے جبکہ شوافع کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ متشابہات کا معنی ومراد اللہ تعالی اور راسخین فی العلم جانتے ہیں والبرابخون فی العلم معطوف ہے اللہ پر اور الا اللہ پر وقف لازم نہیں ہے بلکہ الراسخون فی العلم پر لازم ہے یقولون امنا به الراسخون - یہ حال ہے ۔ ترجمہ ! اس طرح ہوگا کہ متشابہات کا معنی نہیں جانتے مگر اللہ تعالی اور راسخون فی العلم در انحالیکہ وہ کہتے ہیں امنا به کل من عند بنا ۔ وفائدة انزاله ابتلاء الراسخين فى العلم - غرض جواب سوال مقدر ۔ سوال ! ہوتا ہے کہ قرآن پاک کا انزال تو ہدایت کیلئے ہے اور حصول ہدایت معلوم المعنی سے ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مجہول المعنی سے جب متشابہات مجہول المعانی ہیں تو ان سے حصول ہدایت متعذر ہے لہذا ان کا انزال بے فائدہ ہوگا۔ جواب ! شارح نے جواب دیا که انزال متشابہات بے فائدہ نہیں ہے بلکہ باقائدہ ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ ان میں راسخون فی العلم کا امتحان ہے کیونکہ علماء راسخین کی تمنا اور امرمحبوب یہ ہے کہ انکو تمام امور اسرار ورموز کا علم حاصل ہو جائے اور ہر شخص کا امتحان یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اس کو اس کی محبوب و مطلوب شئی کی تحصیل سے روک دیا جائے تو ذات باری تعالی نے متشابہات کا انزال کر کے علماء کا امتحان لیا کہ ان کو ان کے معانی و اسرار کے اندر غور وفکر کرنے سے (جو انکا مطلوب و محبوب ہے) روک دیا ابتلاء و آزمائش کیلئے کہ وہ اللہ کا حکم مان کر اپنی محبوب و مطلوب چیز کو ترک کرتے ہیں اور اپنے نفس کی خواہش کے خلاف کرتے ہیں یا نہ اور یہی طریقہ امتحان ہے کہ ہر شخص کو اس کی محبوب و مطلوب شئی کی تحصیل سے روک دیا جاتا ہے جیسا کہ عند الجہاں علم کا حصول غیر مطلوب و غیر مقصود ہوتا ہے ان کا متمنا و آرزو عدم طلب علم ہے ان کا ابتلاء و امتحان یہ ہوگا کہ ان کو حکم کیا جائے گا علم حاصل کرو۔ تنبیہ اعلی ماهو المذهب کہہ کر شارح تفتازانی نے اپنے مذہب کا اخفاء کیا کما ھو مذہنا نہیں کہا تا کہ اس کو شفی نہ سمجھ لیا جائے نما ھو مذہب . الا جناف بھی نہیں کہا تا کہ اس کو غیر حنفی نہ سمجھ لیا جائے واللہ اعلم بحقیقۃ الحال ودیۃ العباد۔
Misk al-Malih and al-Talwih: A thing that it is not, i.e., striving in knowledge and seeking. Similarly, scholars are tested in terms of settling and leaving... and it is beloved according to [some] because every person's test is against his desire and contrary to his wish. His saying: 'maqsurat' i.e., 'mahbusat' – the commentator explained the meaning of maqsurat. He made the tents of concealment, etc. The purpose of the commentator is to explain the text. The summary is that the author compared the mutashabihat verses to those hidden and confined things upon which tents of structure and concealment are set up, and they surround them such that there is no hope of their appearance. The Hanafi doctrine also is that no one knows the meaning and intent of mutashabihat except Allah the Holy, and in the Holy Qur'an, stopping at 'ثم یعلم تاویلہ الا اللہ' is necessary, and 'والراسخون فی العلم' is a separate sentence. Whereas the Shafi'i doctrine is that Allah and the firmly grounded in knowledge know the meaning and intent of mutashabihat, and 'الراسخون فی العلم' is conjoined to 'اللہ', and stopping at 'الا اللہ' is not necessary; rather stopping at 'الراسخون فی العلم' is necessary. 'یقولون امنا به' – this is a state (hal). Translation: Thus the meaning is that no one knows the interpretation of mutashabihat except Allah and the firmly grounded in knowledge, while they say 'we believe in it, all is from our Lord'. And the benefit of its revelation is the test of the firmly grounded in knowledge. This is the answer to an implied question. Question: The revelation of the Holy Qur'an is for guidance, and obtaining guidance is through known meaning, not through unknown meaning. Since mutashabihat are of unknown meanings, obtaining guidance from them is impossible, so their revelation would be useless. Answer: The commentator replied that the revelation of mutashabihat is not useless; rather it has a benefit, which is that in them is a test for the firmly grounded in knowledge, because the desire and beloved matter of the deeply learned is that they acquire knowledge of all secrets and mysteries. The test of every person is that he is prevented from obtaining his beloved and desired thing. So Allah Almighty, by revealing mutashabihat, tested the scholars by preventing them from pondering over their meanings and secrets (which are their desired and beloved) for the sake of trial, to see whether they obey Allah's command and abandon their beloved and desired thing, and act contrary to their soul's desire or not. And this is the method of testing: that every person is prevented from obtaining his beloved and desired thing. Just as, among the ignorant, obtaining knowledge is not desired or intended, and their wish and desire is not to seek knowledge, their trial will be that they will be commanded to acquire knowledge. Remark: By saying 'according to what is the madhhab', the commentator Taftazani concealed his own madhhab; he did not say 'as is our madhhab' lest it be considered Shafi'i, nor did he say 'as is the madhhab of the Hanafis' lest it be considered non-Hanafi. And Allah knows best the reality of the situation and the duty of the servants.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the interpretation of mutashabihat. The Hanafi position, as explained here, is that the meaning of mutashabihat is known only to Allah, and stopping is required at 'illa Allah' in the verse. The Shafi'is hold that the firmly grounded in knowledge also know. The commentator then addresses the question of the benefit of revealing mutashabihat: it serves as a test for the learned, because their test is being prevented from their beloved pursuit of knowledge. Taftazani is noted to have concealed his own madhhab in his wording.

Key Terms
متشابہات (mutashābihāt): Verses of the Qur'an whose meaning is ambiguous and known only to Allah according to the Hanafi school.
راسخون فی العلم (al-rasikhūn fī al-ʿilm): Those deeply grounded in knowledge; scholars with firm understanding.
تأویل (taʾwīl): Interpretation, especially of ambiguous texts; the ultimate meaning known only to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this text, who knows the meaning of mutashabihat?
A) Only Allah
B) Allah and the firmly grounded in knowledge
C) Only the Prophet
D) All believers

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis hold that only Allah knows the true meaning of mutashabihat, and their revelation serves as a test for the deeply learned.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Resolving the Scope of 'All Ways' in the Definition of I'jaz
A rational argument (dalil aqli) defending the Hanafi interpretation of i'jaz.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the dilemma in interpreting 'جمیع طرق' (all ways) in the definition of i'jaz and apply the Hanafi resolution that i'jaz is established by actual ways and consensus.

Core Idea
I'jaz is proven by actual inability, not by exhausting all potential ways.

The definition of i'jaz as 'more eloquent than all other ways' triggers a critical question: what does 'all ways' mean? A questioner presents two possibilities, both seemingly leading to problems. If only current ways are meant, future opposition might be possible; if potential ways are included, Allah's power to produce a like would negate i'jaz. The Hanafi commentator resolves the dilemma by clarifying that only actualized ways are intended, and i'jaz is established by the actual inability of opponents and consensus, not by an exhaustive list of all possible future expressions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and the contested term
Locate the definition of i'jaz in the passage: 'ان یودی المعنی بطریق ھو ابلغ من جميع الطرق'. The term 'جمیع طرق' (all ways) is the focus of the objection.
2
State the two possibilities for 'جمیع طرق'
The objector proposes two interpretations: (1) only existing actualized ways, or (2) both actual and potential future ways.
These correspond to 'طرق محققة' and 'طرق مقدرة'.
3
Explain why the objector rejects the first possibility
If only current ways are meant, future potential ways might allow opposition, so i'jaz would not be definitively proven.
This is a logical objection: absence of current opposition does not guarantee impossibility.
4
Explain why the objector rejects the second possibility
If potential ways are included, then Allah's ability to produce a like would negate i'jaz, yet consensus holds the Quran is miraculous.
This leads to absurdity (muḥāl), showing the interpretation is invalid.
5
State the Hanafi resolution
The commentator argues that 'جمیع طرق' refers only to actual ways; i'jaz is proven by the actual challenge (tahaddi) and consensus, not by enumerating all possible expressions.
Including potential ways is unnecessary and leads to contradiction.

And here are two investigations. As for the first: In the first investigation, there is an objection mentioned: the objection is that the definition of i'jaz in speech is given as 'that meaning is expressed in a way that is more eloquent than all ways.' The questioner asks: what ways are meant by 'all ways'? There are two possibilities: (1) either 'all ways' means the existing, actualized ways, or (2) the actualized existing ways and the potential future ways. Both are invalid. The first possibility is invalid because if 'all ways' means only current ways, then the inimitability of speech is not proven, because i'jaz requires that opposition and producing its like be impossible. In this case, opposition is possible because there may be a potential way with which opposition could occur and a like could be produced. So taking only current ways is insufficient to prove i'jaz. The second possibility is invalid because if 'all ways' includes both actual and potential ways, then there is no shame in i'jaz? Because then the purpose would be that speech whose opposition and production of like is impossible, and which is more eloquent than all ways, and producing its like is impossible now and in future - such i'jaz is not a condition, otherwise the inimitability of the Book of Allah would cease, because Allah is capable of producing a like of the Quran. From this it is known that among potential ways there is a way by which a like of the Quran could be produced. Yet despite this possibility, the Quran is miraculous by consensus. So it is established that taking 'all ways' to mean both actual and potential ways is not correct. So what is meant by 'all ways besides it' is [something else]. The second investigation: In the second investigation, there is also an objection mentioned. This objection is upon the textual phrase 'and this cannot be except one.' Summary of the objection: you said that i'jaz in speech is only one...
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage presents two scholarly investigations (bahthan) addressing objections to the definition of i'jaz. The first objection concerns the phrase 'all ways' in the definition of i'jaz as 'more eloquent than all other ways.' The questioner identifies a dilemma: if 'all ways' means only currently existing linguistic ways, then i'jaz is not assured because future ways might allow opposition. If it includes both current and potential ways, then i'jaz would be impossible because Allah could produce a like, which would negate the Quran's inimitability. Both horns are invalid. The commentator resolves that the intended meaning is not all ways absolutely, but the specific way of eloquence that is superior to any other actual way. The second objection (incomplete) is on the author's statement 'this cannot be except one,' likely arguing that i'jaz must be singular in its way. Although the text cuts off, the commentator is defending the idea that i'jaz in speech is a single, unique quality despite multiple interpretations of its cause.

Key Terms
جمیع طرق (jami' turuq): All ways (of expression) - debated whether actual only or includes potential.
محققة (muhaqqaqah): Actualized, existing ways of expression.
اعجاز (i'jaz): The miraculous inimitability of the Quran; its inability to be opposed or matched.
معارضہ (mu'aradah): Opposition or matching the Quran in eloquence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it would make i'jaz dependent on future possibilities.
B) Because it does not guarantee impossibility of future opposition.
C) Because it would imply the Quran is not miraculous.
D) Because it contradicts the Quranic challenge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi resolution to the dilemma of 'all ways' is that i'jaz is proven by actual challenge and consensus, not by enumerating all potential expressions.

Dispute on Names of Disciplines: ‘Alam Shakhsi vs ‘Alam Jins
Discussion on the ontological classification of discipline names in Hanafi usul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ‘alam shakhsi and ‘alam jins, and evaluate the two Hanafi positions on the nature of discipline names.

Core Idea
Discipline names like Usul al-Fiqh are proper nouns that apply to a composite whole, not to isolated issues.

In this passage, we explore a subtle but important dispute in Hanafi usul: whether the name of a discipline (such as ‘Usul al-Fiqh’) is a proper noun like ‘Zaid’ or a proper name for a genus. The answer affects how we define and understand the scope of the discipline. We will examine the arguments of two scholars and the key concept of mental determination.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
First, note the two views: Ibn Humam (supported by Taftazani) holds that discipline names are ‘alam shakhsi (proper nouns); Tashid Sharif holds they are ‘alam jins (proper names for a genus).
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
2
Examine the proof for the first position
Ibn Humam's proof: just as ‘Zaid’ applies to the composite whole (not just hand or head), Usul al-Fiqh applies to the totality of issues, not a single issue. The name has personal signs (علامات شخص).
Taftazani supports this by calling Usul al-Fiqh a 'knowledge'.
3
Examine the proof for the second position
Tashid Sharif argues that discipline names involve mental determination (ta'yin dhihni), which is characteristic of ‘alam jins, not ism jins (common noun). Ism jins has no mental determination.
For example, Usul al-Fiqh is defined as 'the universal issues present in minds'.
4
Distinguish the key concept: mental determination
Understand the difference: ism jins denotes a genus without mental individuation; ‘alam jins denotes a genus with mental individuation (like a proper name for a class). Discipline names require such mental determination.
This is the crux of the dispute.
5
Assess the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The dispute affects whether the definition of a discipline is a proper definition (hadd) or a definition by reference (rasm). If it's ‘alam shakhsi, the name points to a specific set; if ‘alam jins, it defines a concept.
The passage does not prefer one, but Taftazani's support suggests the first view is stronger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہوتا۔ مذہب ثامنیعلامہ ابن ہمام کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ اسامی فنون من قبیل ، الاعلام میں یعنی علم شخصی ہیں دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان میں علامات شخص موجود ہیں جس طرح کہ زید کا اطلاق مجموع اجزاء پر ہوتا ہے صرف ہاتھ یا صرف راس پر نہیں ہوتا اسی طرح اصول فقہ کا اطلاق بھی فقط ایک مسئلہ پر نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مجموعہ مسائل پر ہوتا ہے شارح تفتازانی نے واصول الفقہ علم کہ کر اپنی مذہب کی تا پر ئید کی ہے کہ اسامی فنون علم ہوتے ہیں۔ مذہب تالشید سند شریف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ اسامی فنون علم جنس ہیں نہ کہ اسم جنس کیونکہ اہم جنس میں تعیین فی الذان کا لحاظ نہیں ہوتا اور علم جنس میں اس کا لحاظ ہوتا ہے اور اسامی فنون میں تعیین ذہنی کا لحاظ ہوتا ہے۔ مثلا اصول فقہ موضوع ہے۔ للمسائل الحاصلة في الاذہان علی وجہ الكلية الہذا اسامی فنون علم جنس ہیں نہ کہ اسم جنس ۔
Hota. The madhhab of Allamah Ibn Humam is that the names of the disciplines are of the category of proper nouns, i.e., proper nouns. The proof is that in them there are personal signs, just as the application of Zaid is on the total of parts, not only on the hand or only on the head, similarly the application of Usul al-Fiqh is not only on one issue but on the totality of issues. Commentator Taftazani supported his own madhhab by saying that Usul al-Fiqh is a knowledge, that the names of disciplines are knowledge. The madhhab of Tashid Sharif is that the names of disciplines are 'alam jins (proper name for a genus), not ism jins (common noun), because in ism jins there is no consideration of mental determination, but in 'alam jins there is such consideration, and in the names of disciplines mental determination is considered. For example, Usul al-Fiqh is defined as 'for the issues present in minds in a universal manner', therefore the names of disciplines are 'alam jins, not ism jins.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute about the nature of the names of disciplines such as Usul al-Fiqh. The first position, attributed to Allamah Ibn Humam (and supported by Taftazani), holds that these names are 'alam shakhsi (proper nouns), similar to the name 'Zaid'. The proof is that these names apply to a composite set of issues with defining characteristics, not to individual parts. The second position, attributed to Tashid Sharif, holds that they are 'alam jins (proper names for a genus), not ism jins (common nouns). The distinction lies in mental determination: in ism jins, no mental individuation is considered, whereas in 'alam jins it is. Since Usul al-Fiqh is defined by a universal concept embracing all issues meeting that description, it functions as a proper name for a genus. The commentator thus clarifies the ontological status of discipline names as a preliminary to defining the compound term.

Key Terms
علم شخصی ('alam shakhsi): A proper noun that refers to a specific individual or set, like the name Zaid.
اسم جنس (ism jins): A common noun that refers to a genus without mental determination.
علم جنس ('alam jins): A proper noun for a genus, considering mental determination.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Allamah Ibn Humam, why are names of disciplines like Usul al-Fiqh considered proper nouns ('alam shakhsi)?
A) Because they apply to individual parts like hands and head.
B) Because they have personal signs and apply to the totality of issues, not just one issue.
C) Because they are derived from other words through derivation (ishtiqaq).
D) Because they are common nouns (ism jins) that denote a genus.

Key Takeaway
Discipline names like Usul al-Fiqh are either proper nouns (with personal signs) or proper names for a genus (with mental determination), a distinction with implications for definition.

Definition of Asl and Refutation of Taftazani's Objection
Explaining and rebutting Taftazani's objection to Razi's definition of asl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Taftazani's objection to the author of Al-Tawdih is considered invalid in the Hanafi usul tradition, and distinguish between nominal and real definitions regarding the requirement of coextensiveness (itrad).

Core Idea
Nominal definitions for conventional composites do not require coextensiveness; Taftazani's objection confuses them with real definitions.

In this passage from the commentary on Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih, we encounter a classic usul dispute over the definition of the term 'asl' (source/origin). Imam Razi defined 'asl' as 'muhtaj ilayh' (that which is needed), but this definition faces a critique from the author of Al-Tawdih. Taftazani, in his Talwih, objects to the author's framing, arguing that the definition's nominal nature is irrelevant. We will trace the Hanafi response, which clarifies the role of nominal definitions and ultimately upholds the critique of Razi's definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
What is the precise point of disagreement between Taftazani and the author of Al-Tawdih regarding the definition of 'asl'? Taftazani claims the author's statement that the definition is nominal is unnecessary because any definition, real or nominal, must be coextensive.
Taftazani's position: definition must be mutually convertible.
2
Understand the Hanafi rejoinder
The commentator provides six responses. Identify the central argument: nominal definitions of conventional composites do not require coextensiveness as a condition of validity. The author's statement serves to clarify the type of definition, not to assert a condition.
Key: ta'rif ismi (nominal definition) vs. ta'rif haqiqi (real definition).
3
Examine the five-fold classification of muhtaj ilayh
The passage divides 'that which is needed' into five types: material cause, formal cause, efficient cause, final cause, and condition. Only the material cause is actually called 'asl' in linguistic usage.
This enumeration shows why Razi's definition fails: it does not specify which type of muhtaj ilayh is meant.
4
Apply the classification to evaluate Razi's definition
Test Razi's definition ('asl = muhtaj ilayh') against the five types. The definition applies to all five, but the defined term 'asl' applies only to material cause. Thus the definition is not coextensive.
Failure of itrad (coextensiveness) renders the definition defective for either nominal or real definitions if coextensiveness were required, but the Hanafi position is that for nominal definitions it is not a defect; yet here the definition fails even on its own terms because it does not match linguistic usage.
5
Conclude the role of definition in qiyas
In usul al-fiqh, the definition of 'asl' determines how qiyas is structured. Hanafi usul restricts 'asl' to the original case in analogical reasoning, which must be a material cause. This precise definition prevents over-application of qiyas.
The practical consequence: only material causes can serve as 'asl' for analogical extension.

شارح کے اعتراض کے متعدد جوابات دیے گئے ہیں (۱) مقصود مصنف تعریف لفظی کی نفی ہے کہ تعریف اصل تعریف آئی ہے تعریف لفظی نہیں ہے کیونکہ لفظی میں اطراد شرط نہیں ہے (۲) یہ کلام توضیح کیلئے ہے کہ اصل کی تعریف اسمی ہے اور اس کا اسمی ہونا اس اعتبار سے ہے کہ یہ مرکب اعتباری کی تعریف ہے اور اس سے ماہیت اعتبار یہ حاصل ہوتی ہے یہ تعریف اسمی اس اعتبار سے نہیں ہے کہ اسمیں موضوع لہ کو لفظ اشہر کے ساتھ بیان کیا گیا ہو جیسا کہ بعض حضرات کا قول ہے تو مقصود مصنف توضیح اور تردید نظریہ بعض حضرات ہے۔ (۳) مقصود مصنف جواب سوال ہے کیونکہ ماقبل میں تعریف کی دو قسمیں ذکر ہوئیں حقیقی و اسمی تو سائل نے سوال کیا تعریف الاصل من ای قسم تو مصنف نے جواب دیالا شک الخ تو مقصود جواب سوال ہے نہ یہ کہ اطراد اسمی میں شرط ہے اور عدم اطراد صرف اسی کیلئے مفسد ہے (۴) اس عبارت کے بعد فساد تعریف کا ذکر ہے اور اس عبارت سے پہلے تعریف کی دو قسموں تعریف حقیقی و اسی کا بیان ہے اور قول ولا شک بیان سابق کا حصہ وتتمہ ہے یہ مابعد کا حصہ نہیں ہے تو مقصد یہ ہوگا کہ تعریف حقیقی واسی میں سے اصل کی تعریف اسی سے حقیقی نہیں ہے لہذا اسکو بیان فساد تعریف میں کوئی دخل نہیں ہے تفتازانی نے بیچ فرمایا ہے کہ لا دخل له فی بیان فساد التعریف (۵) یہ قول در اصل قول سابق کا نتیجہ ہے کیونکہ کلام سابق تمہید تھی که تعریف الاصل حقیقی ہے یا اسی ، فقسم التعريف الى قسمين ثم قال بعد التمهيد ولا شك ان تعريف الاصل اسمى نتيجة لما سبق تو یہ قول فائدہ سے خالی نہیں (۶) قول مصنف صغری ہے اور کبری محذوف ہے تقدیر عبارت اس طرح ہوگی ولا شك أن تعريف الاصل اسمى (مغرى) والتعريف الاسمى يجب فيه الاطراد ( کبری) ۔ نتیجہ ہوگا ۔ فتعريف الاصـل يـجـب فيـه الالـطـرادف التعريف الذي ذكر الخ میں اس نتیجہ کی طرف اشارہ ہے خلاصہ ایں کہ عبارہ مذکورہ ماتن نے فائدہ اور ضرورت کے تحت ذکر کی ہے تو اشکال تفتازانی غلط ہے ففى الجملة تعريف الاصل بالمحتاج اليه غير مطرد

یہاں سے شارح اعتراض مصنف علی صاحب الحصول (رازی) کی توضیح و تشریح کر رہے ہیں خلاصہ یہ کہ امام رازی نے اصل کی تعریف محتاج الیہ کے ساتھ کی ہے لیکن یہ تعریف غیر مطر د اور غیر مانع ہے کیونکہ مطرد ہونے اور مقصود ہوگا اول کو فائل ( علت فاعلیہ ) کہتے ہیں مثال نجار سریر کیلئے ثانی کو غایت ( علت غائیہ ) کہتے ہیں مثال الجلوس على السرير اگر محتاج الیہ ہوکر ان اشیاء اربعہ مذکورہ کے علاوہ ہے تو اسے شرط کہا جاتا Misk al-Maleeh. Commentary on Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih. The description of neediness of another is considered (as is the view of al-Razi). Therefore, when the essence of 'asl' is a conventional composite, its definition will be like that. Because it has been mentioned that definitions of conventional realities are nominal definitions, and this has no bearing on explaining the corruption of the definition. The intent of the commentator Taftazani is to object to the author. The objection: The author's statement 'and there is no doubt that the definition of 'asl' is a nominal definition' is unnecessary and superfluous. Because the author's purpose is to explain the corruption of Imam al-Razi's definition of 'asl' (al-muhtaj ilayh). The reason for corruption is lack of coextensiveness (not being inclusive) and not being exclusive, which corrupt any definition, whether real or nominal. Since the author's expression indicates that the definition of 'asl' is nominal, therefore coextensiveness is necessary for it, and lack of it is corrupting, whereas it is not so. Hence the author's expression is unnecessary. If for a nominal definition coextensiveness were necessary and lack of it corrupting only for nominal, then it would have been necessary to prove that the definition of 'asl' is nominal, so that lack of coextensiveness would be corrupting for it. Response: Multiple responses have been given to the commentator's objection: (1) The author's purpose is to negate a verbal definition, that the definition of 'asl' is a nominal definition, not a verbal one, because coextensiveness is not a condition in verbal definitions. (2) This statement is for clarification: that the definition of 'asl' is nominal, and its being nominal is in the sense that it is a definition of a conventional composite, and from it the conventional essence is obtained. This nominal definition is not in the sense that the defined term is explained with a more famous word, as some say. So the author's purpose is clarification and refutation of the view of some. (3) The author's purpose is to answer a question, because previously two types of definition were mentioned: real and nominal. The questioner asked: 'Which type is the definition of 'asl'?' The author answered: 'There is no doubt...', so the purpose is to answer the question, not that coextensiveness is a condition in nominal definitions and lack of it is corrupting only for that. (4) After this expression, the corruption of the definition is mentioned, and before it, the two types of definition, real and nominal, were explained. The statement 'and there is no doubt' is part and completion of the previous discourse, not part of what follows. So the purpose is that the definition of 'asl' among real and nominal is not real, therefore it has no bearing on explaining the corruption of the definition. Taftazani said in between: 'It has no bearing on explaining the corruption of the definition.' (5) This statement is actually a result of the previous statement, because the previous speech was a preamble whether the definition of 'asl' is real or nominal. So he divided definition into two types, then after the preamble he said: 'And there is no doubt that the definition of 'asl' is nominal' as a result of what preceded. So this statement is not devoid of benefit. (6) The author's statement is the minor premise, and the major premise is implied. The construction of the statement would be: 'And there is no doubt that the definition of 'asl' is nominal' (minor). 'And a nominal definition requires coextensiveness' (major). The conclusion: 'Therefore the definition of 'asl' requires coextensiveness.' In the definition he mentioned [later], there is an indication of this conclusion. Summary: The author (matn) mentioned the stated expression for benefit and necessity, so Taftazani's objection is wrong. In summary, the definition of 'asl' by al-muhtaj ilayh is not coextensive. From here, the commentator is explaining and clarifying the author's objection to the author of al-Husul (Razi). Summary: Imam Razi defined 'asl' as 'muhtaj ilayh' (that which is needed). But this definition is not coextensive and not exclusive, because the meaning of being coextensive and exclusive is that wherever the definition applies, the defined applies. This meaning of coextensiveness is not present in Razi's definition, because there are many instances to which the definition applies, e.g., (1) efficient cause, (2) formal cause, (3) final cause, (4) condition. All these are muhtaj ilayh, the definition applies to them, but the defined, i.e., the word 'asl', does not apply to them, because the word 'asl' is used only for material cause. So it is not found that 'whenever the definition applies, the defined applies'. Therefore Razi's definition is not coextensive. Because that which a thing needs (muhtaj ilayh) has five types. The commentator is explaining the proof of this enumeration. Summary: The thing on which another thing depends for its existence and realization, that thing (muhtaj ilayh) is either inside the dependent thing or outside. If inside, then two possibilities: either the dependent thing gets existence in potentiality from it, or in actuality. If potentiality, it is called material cause, like wood for a bed. If actuality, it is called formal cause, like the bed-like form for the bed. If the muhtaj ilayh is outside the dependent thing, then two possibilities: either the dependent thing gets existence from it (efficient cause) or the dependent thing exists for the sake of it (final cause). The first is called efficient cause, e.g., carpenter for the bed. The second is called final cause, e.g., sitting on the bed. If the muhtaj ilayh is other than these four, it is called condition, e.g., the carpenter's tools and the wood's suitability for the bed. So these become five types. Some have presented the enumeration in another way, which is more famous: cause (muhtaj ilayh) is either prior to the effect or posterior. If prior, then either inside the effect or outside. If prior and inside the effect, it is material cause; if prior and outside the effect, it is efficient cause. If cause is posterior, it is also two: inside the effect or outside. The first is formal cause, the second is final cause. These are four. The author (Tawdih) added condition to them, so these become five. The purpose is that of these five types, only one type is such that the defined (asl) applies to it linguistically, and that is material cause, as in 'the origin of this bed is wood'. Besides that, the definition (muhtaj ilayh) applies to the remaining four types, because they are all types of muhtaj ilayh (as known in the explanation of enumeration), but the defined does not apply to them, because they are not called 'asl'. Hence some...
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the definition of the term 'asl' (source/origin) in legal theory. The commentator (sharh) first recounts Taftazani's objection to the author of Al-Tawdih (probably Sadr al-Shariah) regarding the author's statement that the definition of 'asl' is nominal. Taftazani argues that this statement is unnecessary because the purpose is to show the corruption of Imam Razi's definition of 'asl' as 'muhtaj ilayh' (that which is needed). Taftazani claims that coextensiveness (itrad) is required for any definition, whether real or nominal, so the author's emphasis on 'asl' being nominal is pointless. The commentator then provides six responses defending the author. The key point is that nominal definitions (isma'iyyah) are of a conventional composite, and their validity does not require coextensiveness in the same way as real definitions (haqiqiyyah). The author's statement clarifies that the definition is nominal, thus coextensiveness is not a condition for its validity, contrary to Taftazani's assumption. The second part of the passage explains why Razi's definition fails on its own terms. By analyzing the five categories of 'muhtaj ilayh' (material, formal, efficient, final causes, and condition), the commentator shows that only the material cause (al-illat al-madiyyah) is actually called 'asl'. The other four categories are technically 'muhtaj ilayh' but are not termed 'asl', so Razi's definition is neither coextensive nor exclusive. This analysis relies on a detailed classification of causes derived from Aristotelian philosophy but adapted for usul al-fiqh. The Hanafi position, as defended by the author of Al-Tawdih, is that Razi's definition is indeed flawed, but Taftazani's objection to the author's wording is unfounded because the author was correctly identifying the definition as nominal rather than real.

Key Terms
تعریف اسمی (ta'rif ismi): A nominal definition that explains the meaning of a term, especially for conventional composites, without necessarily stating the essence.
اطراد (itrad): Coextensiveness: the property of a definition that applies to all instances of the definiendum.
علت مادی (illat maddiyyah): Material cause: that from which something is made and which gives potential existence (e.g., wood for a bed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many types of 'muhtaj ilayh' (that which is needed) are enumerated?
A) Two
B) Four
C) Five
D) Six

Key Takeaway
Taftazani's objection to the author of Al-Tawdih is invalid because nominal definitions of conventional composites, like that of 'asl', do not require coextensiveness; the real flaw in Razi's definition is that it includes causes that are not conventionally called 'asl'.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
6 min
Critique of the Definition of Rational Dependence
Taftazani's objection to Sadr al-Shariah's definition of ibtina' 'aqli and its refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct definition of rational dependence (al-ibtina' al-'aqli) according to Sadr al-Shariah and evaluate Taftazani's objection.

Core Idea
Rational dependence is the intellectual arrangement of one thing on another, not merely a ruling on its proof.

In this passage, we encounter a classic usul dispute over the definition of rational dependence (al-ibtina' al-'aqli). Taftazani objects that the author's definition fails to cover thought's dependence on known matters. The reply reveals a crucial distinction: the purported definition is only an example. Understanding this distinction sharpens your ability to differentiate between a definition and an illustration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting definitions
Taftazani claims the author defined rational dependence as 'the arrangement of a ruling on its proof' (tartub al-hukm 'ala dalilih), which does not cover thought depending on known matters. The reply asserts that the true definition is broader: 'the arrangement of one thing on another in the intellect' (tartub al-shay' 'ala shay' fi al-'aql).
2
Analyze Taftazani's objection
Taftazani argues that thought is not a ruling and known matters are not proof, so the definition is not comprehensive. Understand the logical structure of his objection.
He is applying the definition strictly.
3
Examine the reply
The responder points out that Taftazani himself had admitted that the expression is only an example, not the definition. Therefore his objection is self-contradictory.
This is a form of ad hominem but also a substantive point about the scope of definition.
4
Extract the actual definition
The correct definition is 'tartub al-shay' 'ala shay' fi al-'aql' (arrangement of one thing on another in the intellect). Apply it to the case of thought and known matters to see it works.
This definition is more inclusive.
5
Understand the significance
Knowing the actual definition prevents misapplication in usul reasoning. It shows the importance of distinguishing between a definition and an example.

معلومہ علت صور یہ مفکر علت فاعلیہ اور ایصال الی المحمول علت غائیہ ہے جب امور معلومہ مادہ اور اصل ہیں تو فکر کا ان پر ابتناء ہوگا لیکن ابتناء کی دونوں قسموں میں سے کوئی قسم نہیں بن سکتی فکر کا ابتناء امور معلومہ پر نہ تو حسی ہے دھو ظا ہر اور نہ ابتناء عقلی ہے ، جفسیر المصنف کیونکہ مصنف نے ابتاء عقلی کی تعریف کی ہے ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ اور فکر کا ابتناء علی امور معلومہ یہ ترتب الحکم علی دلیلہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ فکر حکم نہیں ہے اور امور معلومہ اس کیلئے دلیل نہیں ہے لہذا آپ کی تعریف جامع نہیں ہے۔ جواب ! شارح تفتازانی کا یہ اشکال لغو اور بے سود ہے دراصل تفتازانی نے یہ تہیہ کر رکھا ہے کہ مصنف کی ہر بات کی تردید کرنی ہے اس لیے وہ ہر جائز و نا جائز اشکال کرتا ہے اور یہ بھی نہیں سوچتا کہ یہ میری اپنی کلام کے خلاف ہے . اشکال مذکور بھی اسی کا ایک نمونہ ہے شارح تفتازانی ماقبل میں کہ چکے ہیں۔ والحق ان ترتب الحكم على دليله لاتصلح تغير اللابناء العقلى وانما ھومثال لہ، خود اعتراف کر چکے ہیں کہ ترتب احکم ابتنا عقلی کی تفسیر و تعریف نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ اس کی مثال ہے ابتنا عقلی کی تعریف اور ہے، ترتب الشئی علی شئی فی العقل اور یہ تعریف ترتب الفکر علی امور معلومہ پر بالکل صادق آرہی ہے لہذا تعریف مصنف جامع و منعکس ہے اور اعتراض شارح لغو ہے۔
The known matters are material cause, the intellectual is efficient cause, and reaching the predicate is final cause. When the known matters are matter and principle, then thought depends on them. But thought's dependence on known matters cannot be one of the two types: it is neither sensory, for it is apparent, nor rational dependence, according to the author's interpretation. Because the author defined rational dependence as 'the arrangement of the ruling on its proof', and thought's dependence on known matters is not that, because thought is not a ruling and known matters are not its proof. Hence your definition is not comprehensive. Reply: Taftazani's objection is frivolous and useless. In fact, Taftazani has resolved to refute everything the author says, so he makes every permissible and impermissible objection, not caring that it contradicts his own words. This objection is one example. The commentator Taftazani has previously admitted: 'The truth is that the arrangement of the ruling on its proof is not a definition of rational dependence; it is only an example of it.' He himself has admitted that 'arrangement of the ruling' is not the interpretation and definition of rational dependence but its example. The definition of rational dependence is something else: 'the arrangement of one thing on another in the intellect'. And this definition applies exactly to the arrangement of thought on known matters. Therefore the author's definition is comprehensive and reversible, and the commentator's objection is frivolous.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between the commentator Taftazani and the author (likely Sadr al-Shariah) over the definition of 'rational dependence' (al-ibtina' al-'aqli). Taftazani objects that the author's definition—'the arrangement of the ruling on its proof'—does not cover the case of thought (fikr) depending on known matters, since thought is not a ruling and known matters are not its proof. Thus the definition is not comprehensive. The responder (the author of the commentary) dismisses Taftazani's objection as frivolous, pointing out that Taftazani himself had previously admitted that the said expression is not the definition but merely an example. The true definition of rational dependence is 'the arrangement of one thing on another in the intellect' (tartub al-shay' 'ala shay' fi al-'aql). This definition applies to thought depending on known matters. Therefore the author's definition (when understood as an example) is in fact comprehensive and reversible, and Taftazani's objection fails.

Key Terms
الابتنا العقلي (al-ibtina' al-'aqli): The arrangement of one thing on another in the intellect (ترتب الشئی علی شئی فی العقل).
ترتب الحكم على دليله (tartub al-hukm 'ala dalilih): The arrangement of a ruling on its proof; here stated as an example, not the actual definition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the actual definition of rational dependence (al-ibtina' al-'aqli)?
A) The arrangement of a ruling on its proof.
B) The arrangement of thought on known matters.
C) The arrangement of one thing on another in the intellect.
D) The sensory dependence of thought on known matters.

Key Takeaway
Rational dependence is the intellectual arrangement of one thing on another; the common phrase 'arrangement of a ruling on its proof' is only an example.

Five Probabilities for 'Ma Laha wa Ma Alayha' in Fiqh Definition
Analyzing five interpretations of the phrase in fiqh definition and selecting comprehensive ones

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate the five interpretations of 'ma laha wa ma alayha' in the Hanafi definition of fiqh, and explain why the Hanafi school includes beliefs and inner states.

Core Idea
Fiqh in the Hanafi school is not limited to actions—it encompasses beliefs and inner states, as reflected in the comprehensive interpretation of 'ma laha wa ma alayha'.

The classic definition of fiqh is 'knowledge of what is for and against the self' (al-ilm bi ma laha wa ma alayha). This phrase is open to interpretation. The passage from the commentary explores five possible meanings, evaluating which ones cover all categories of acts and leaves. It then extends the discussion to show that 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is general enough to include beliefs (i'tiqadiyat), inner states (wijdaniyat), and actions (amaliyat). This reflects the broader Hanafi conception of fiqh, evidenced by Imam Abu Hanifa naming theology as 'al-fiqh al-akbar'.

Guided Path
1
Understand the five probabilities
List the five interpretations of 'ma laha wa ma alayha' as given in the text: (1) punishment and non-punishment, (2) reward and non-reward, (3) permissibility and obligation, (4) permissibility and prohibition, (5) permissibility and prohibition (the fifth is actually the same as the fourth? Wait, the text lists: first: punishment and non-punishment; second: reward and non-reward; third: permissibility and obligation; fourth: permissibility and prohibition; fifth: permissibility and prohibition? But careful: the passage mentions a fourth and fifth differently. Actually, re-reading: first three are under condition of la li-naf and ala li-darar. Fourth and fifth are different. The passage states: fourth probability: ma laha = ma yajuzu laha, ma alayha = ma yajibu alayha; fifth: ma laha = ma yajuzu laha, ma alayha = ma yuhramu alayha. So there are five distinct probabilities. The student should enumerate them clearly.
Probabilities 1-3 use reward/punishment framework; 4 uses obligation; 5 uses prohibition.
2
Assess comprehensiveness
For each probability, determine which categories of acts (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.) and leaves (tark) are included or excluded. The author marks probabilities 2, 3, and 5 as comprehensive (jami' jami' al-aqsam). Note why probability 4 is not comprehensive.
Probability 4 excludes forbidden act, makruh tahrimi, and tark wajib from both sides.
3
Identify the preferred probability
The author states that among the five, the ones without 'wasit' (intermediary) are preferable, i.e., those that directly cover all divisions. These are probabilities 2, 3, and 5. Recognize that all three can be expressed as reward/non-reward, punishment/non-punishment, or permissibility/prohibition.
The preference is based on inclusivity, not on any particular theological stance.
4
Extend the analysis to scope of fiqh
The author then argues that 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is general and can cover beliefs, inner states, and actions. This is a linguistic argument: the phrase itself does not restrict to actions. The Hanafi school, particularly Imam Abu Hanifa, did not add the condition of 'amal in the definition, thus including i'tiqadiyat and wijdaniyat.
Evidence: Imam Abu Hanifa's naming of theology as 'al-fiqh al-akbar'.
5
Contrast with other schools
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) restrict fiqh to practical acts ('amaliyat) by adding the condition of 'amal. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi, theological methodology is part of fiqh; in others, it is separate.
This reflects a difference in the scope of the discipline.

Leaving of recommended (6), leaving of permissible (7), leaving of abominable-tanzihi (8), leaving of forbidden (9), leaving of abominable-tahrimi (10). This probability is comprehensive of all divisions. Third probability: that 'ma laha' means reward and 'alayha' means non-reward. In that case, obligatory act and recommended act are included in 'yuthabu alayha', and the remaining ten divisions (four acts and six leaves) are included in 'la yuthab'. This probability is also comprehensive of all divisions. These three probabilities are on the condition that 'la' in 'laha' is for benefit and 'ala' in 'alayha' is for harm. Fourth probability: that 'ma laha' means what is permissible for it and 'ma alayha' means what is obligatory upon it. According to this probability, except for forbidden act and abominable-tahrimi, the four types of acts (recommended, permissible, obligatory, abominable-tanzihi) and except for leaving of obligatory, the five types of leaves (leaving recommended, leaving permissible, leaving forbidden, leaving abominable-tahrimi, leaving abominable-tanzihi) - all these are included in 'yajuzu laha'. And obligatory act, leaving forbidden, leaving abominable-tahrimi are included in 'yajibu alayha'. And forbidden act, abominable-tahrimi act, and leaving obligatory are not included in either 'yajuzu laha' nor 'yajibu alayha' because they are neither permissible nor obligatory. This probability is not comprehensive of all divisions. Fifth probability: that 'ma laha' means what is permissible for it and 'ma alayha' means what is forbidden upon it. In this case, (1) forbidden act, (2) abominable-tahrimi, (3) leaving obligatory - these three are included in 'yuhramu alayha'. Besides these, obligatory act, recommended act, permissible act, abominable-tanzihi act, leaving recommended, leaving permissible, leaving forbidden, leaving abominable-tahrimi, leaving abominable-tanzihi - all these are included in 'yajuzu laha'. This probability is also comprehensive of all divisions. When you have known these five probabilities in detail, the author says: among these five probabilities, the one that is more preferable is that which has no intermediary, i.e., which includes all divisions. Those are three probabilities: (1) second probability (that 'ma laha wa ma alayha' means punishment and non-punishment), (2) third probability (reward and non-reward), (3) last probability (permissibility and prohibition). Since these three probabilities are comprehensive of all divisions, therefore it is more preferable to interpret 'ma laha wa ma alayha' accordingly. Then, 'ma laha wa ma alayha' - the author says that the word 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is general; it includes beliefs (i'tiqadiyat) like obligation of faith etc., and inner states (wijdaniyat) like inner ethics and qualities of the soul such as tasawwuf, zuhd, patience, contentment, presence of heart in prayer, etc., and acts of worship and transactions (amaliyat) like prayer, fasting, sale, and similar. If 'ma laha wa ma alayha' pertains to beliefs, then it is called 'ilm al-kalam; if from the category of inner states and ethics, then it is called 'ilm al-akhlaq and 'ilm al-tasawwuf; if from the category of actions, then it is called 'ilm al-fiqh. So 'ma laha wa ma alayha' includes all three sciences. If the purpose is to define only technical fiqh (fiqh istilahi) from 'ma laha wa ma alayha', then it is necessary to add the condition of 'amal (action) so that beliefs and inner states are excluded. And if the purpose is to define absolute fiqh from 'ma laha wa ma alayha' which includes all three, then the condition of 'amal is not added. Thus, Imam Abu Hanifa did not add the condition of 'amal because he included all three in fiqh. This is why Imam Abu Hanifa named the science of kalam as 'al-fiqh al-akbar'. From this, it is understood that 'ilm al-kalam is included in fiqh according to him.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the phrase 'ma laha wa ma alayha' (what is for it and what is against it) from the classic definition of fiqh (knowledge of what is for and against the self). The author presents five possible interpretations of this phrase, evaluating which ones are comprehensive (jami') of all categories of actions and which are not. The five probabilities are based on different meanings of 'la' and 'ala' (for benefit or harm) and different scopes (reward/punishment, permissibility/obligation, permissibility/prohibition). After listing them, the author states that the most preferable are those that include all divisions without exclusion (i.e., second, third, and fifth). Then the author extends the discussion to show that 'ma laha wa ma alayha' is general and can include beliefs, inner states, and actions. The Hanafi school, particularly Imam Abu Hanifa, includes all three in the definition of fiqh, hence he did not restrict fiqh to practical acts. This is evidenced by his naming of theology as 'al-fiqh al-akbar' (the greater fiqh). The passage thus clarifies the comprehensive scope of fiqh in the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
ما لها وما عليها (ma laha wa ma alayha): The phrase meaning 'what is for it and what is against it' referring to the rulings applicable to the self.
جامع جميع الاقسام (jami' jami' al-aqsam): Comprehensive of all categories of acts and leaves.
امام ابو حنیفہ (Imam Abu Hanifa): Founder of the Hanafi school; named theology as 'al-fiqh al-akbar'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of fiqh, rooted in the general phrase 'ma laha wa ma alayha', encompasses beliefs, inner states, and actions, reflecting a comprehensive legal worldview.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

The Makruh Tahrimi Dispute: Imam Muhammad vs. the Shaykhayn
Explaining the dispute on makruh tahrimi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the definition of makruh tahrimi and explain the logical basis for each division.

Core Idea
Makruh tahrimi's legal status is disputed: Imam Muhammad views it as prohibited; the Shaykhayn view it as permissible but blameworthy.

This passage from Taftazani's Al-Talwih explains the division of actions into twelve categories and highlights an internal Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn on the definition of makruh tahrimi. The dispute centers on whether makruh tahrimi falls under 'prohibition of the act' or under 'permissible but close to forbidden'. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for accurately applying Hanafi ahkam.

Guided Path
1
Understand the logical division of actions
The passage presents two logical trees for classifying the actions of a mukallaf. Identify the branches: actions are either equal (mubah) or one side is preponderant. If preponderant, it is either action or abandonment. Each branch leads to a specific ruling (wajib, mandub, makruh tanzihi, haram, makruh tahrimi).
Focus on the point where the two divisions diverge: the treatment of makruh tahrimi.
2
Compare the two divisions
Imam Muhammad's division: If the act is prohibited, the proof is either qat'i (haram) or zanni (makruh tahrimi). The Shaykhayn's division: If the act is not prohibited, it is either close to permissible (makruh tanzihi) or close to forbidden (makruh tahrimi).
Note that for Imam Muhammad, makruh tahrimi is a type of prohibition; for the Shaykhayn, it is not prohibited but blameworthy.
3
Analyze the basis of difference
Imam Muhammad uses the strength of the proof (thubut) to distinguish haram from makruh tahrimi. The Shaykhayn use the concept of proximity (aqrab ila al-hillah vs. aqrab ila al-hurmah) and consider the punishment: fire for haram, blame and possible deprivation of intercession for makruh tahrimi.
4
Apply the dispute to a case
Suppose a person consumes a substance that is prohibited by a weak (zanni) hadith. According to Imam Muhammad, this is makruh tahrimi: the act is impermissible and the person is sinful. According to the Shaykhayn, it is not prohibited but blameworthy; the person may be deprived of intercession.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) affects the ruling on sin and punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

علیہ میں داخل کیا ہے کا لحرام اور یہی اما محمد کی رائے ہے کہ وہ مکروہ تحریمی کو منع عن الفعل اور حرام کے ساتھ شامل کرتے ہیں شیخین کے مذہب کے مطابق دلیل حصر اس طرح ہے مایا تی به المكلف متساوی الطرفین ( فعل و ترک) ہوگا یا نہ اول مباح ہے اگر متساوی الطرفین نہیں ہے تو دو صورتیں ہیں جانب فعل راج ہوگی یا جانب ترک اگر جانب فعل راجح و اولی ہے تو دو صورتیں ہیں ترک سے منع کیا گیا ہوگایانہ اگر کیا گیا ہے تو واجب دور نہ مندوب اگر جانب ترک اولی ہے تو دو صورتیں ہیں فعل سے منع کیا گیا ہوگا یا نہ اگر منع کیا گیا ہے تو حرام اگر فعل سے منع نہیں کیا گیا تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو اقرب الی الحلت ہوگا یا اقرب الی الحرمت اگر اقرب الی الحلت ہے تو مکروہ تنزیہی ہے اقرب الی الحلت ہونے کا مقصد یہ ہے کہ اس کے فاعل کو عقاب اور سزا تو نہ ہوگی البتہ اس کے تارک کو ادنی اور تھوڑ اسا ثواب ہوگا اور اگر اقرب الی الحرمت کیونکہ مصنف نے مکروہ تحریمی کو لا يجوز فعله بل يجب تركه ويعاقب على فعلہ میں درج کیا ہے خلاصہ اختلاف امام محمد شیخین یہی ہے کہ مام مکروہ تحریمی کو لا يجوز فعل او منع عن الفعل میں داخل کرتے ہیں کا لحرام اورشیخین اس کو یجوز فعلہ میں داخل کرتے ہیں۔ سوال ! شارح کا یہ قول کہ مرتکب مکروہ تحریمی شفاعت سے محروم ہو جائے گا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ ارتکاب مکروہ تحریمی تو گناہ صغیرہ ہے گناہ کبیرہ کا ارتکاب کرنے (۴) حرمان شفاعت سے شفاعت الملئکہ مراد . ہے جیسا کہ حدیث میں ہے نیک آدمی کی دعا کی قبولیت کیلئے فرشتے سفارش کرتے ہیں اور اسکی دعا پر آمین کہتے ہیں مرتکب مکروہ
The divisions are twelve because of [the saying] 'what the obligated person does' etc. The commentator Taftazani explains the proof for the twelve divisions of the actions of the obligated person. Since there is a difference between the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad in the definition of makruh tahrimi, there is also a difference in the basis of the division. According to Imam's opinion, the proof of the division is as follows: the action of the obligated human is either both the act and its abandonment are equal, or one of them is preponderant. If both are equal, it is called mubah. If there is a preponderant side, then either the side of action is preponderant or the side of abandonment. If the side of action is preponderant, there are two possibilities: the abandonment has been prohibited or not. If it has been prohibited, it is wajib; if not, it is mandub. If the side of abandonment is preponderant, there are two possibilities: the act has been prohibited or not. If not, it is makruh tanzihi. If the act has been prohibited, then there are two possibilities: the prohibition is by a definitive proof or by a speculative proof. If by definitive, it is called haram; if by speculative, it is called makruh tahrimi. According to Imam Muhammad's school, makruh tahrimi is included in 'prohibition of the act', meaning it is not permissible to do it, rather it is obligatory to leave it. So both haram and makruh tahrimi are included in the prohibition of the act; the difference between them is only in terms of thubut (establishment): haram has prohibition by definitive proof, and makruh tahrimi by speculative proof. And he explained that here, the basis of division according to Imam Muhammad is appropriate, because the author included makruh tanzihi in 'its act is permissible' and makruh tahrimi in 'its act is not permissible, rather it is obligatory to leave it and one is punished for it' like haram. And this is the opinion of Imam Muhammad, that he includes makruh tahrimi in the prohibition of the act along with haram. According to the school of the Shaykhayn, the proof of the division is as follows: what the obligated person does is either the two sides (act and abandonment) are equal or not. The first is mubah. If the two sides are not equal, there are two possibilities: the side of action is preponderant or the side of abandonment. If the side of action is preponderant and preferable, there are two possibilities: the abandonment has been prohibited or not. If it has been prohibited, it is wajib; otherwise, mandub. If the side of abandonment is preferable, there are two possibilities: the act has been prohibited or not. If prohibited, it is haram. If the act is not prohibited, it is either close to permissible or close to forbidden. If close to permissible, it is makruh tanzihi, meaning the doer will not be punished, but the abandoner will get a little reward. If close to forbidden, it is called makruh tahrimi, meaning the doer will not be punished with the fire, but he will be deserving of blame, and some other punishment will be given, like the commentator gave the example of deprivation of intercession (shafa'ah). So according to the opinion and school of the Shaykhayn, makruh tahrimi is included in 'its act is permissible', and its doer is not deserving of punishment by fire. This all is contrary to this place, because the author included makruh tahrimi in 'its act is not permissible, rather it is obligatory to leave and one is punished for its act'. The summary of the difference between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn is that Imam Muhammad includes makruh tahrimi in the prohibition of the act like haram, and the Shaykhayn include it in the permissible. Objection: The commentator's statement that the doer of makruh tahrimi will be deprived of intercession is incorrect, because committing makruh tahrimi is a minor sin, and the committer of a major sin will not be deprived of intercession, so how can the committer of a minor sin be deprived? And in the hadith: 'My intercession is for the major sins of my community.' Answers: Several answers have been given to this objection. (1) The meaning of 'deprivation of intercession' is not the intercession of the Prophet, but rather that this person is deprived of interceding for sinners, because in the hadith, the believers will intercede for one another on the Day of Judgment, so the doer of makruh tahrimi will be deprived of interceding. (2) Deprivation of intercession has two types: perpetual and temporary. Here temporary deprivation is meant, that the Prophet's intercession for the doer of makruh tahrimi will be delayed. (3) The Prophet's intercession has many types: one intercession is for removal from the fire, one is for raising ranks. The committer of major sins and makruh tahrimi will be deserving of the first, but deprived of the second, i.e., intercession for elevation of ranks will not be made. (4) Deprivation of intercession means the intercession of angels, as in the hadith: angels intercede for the acceptance of a good person's prayer and say 'Amin' to his prayer. The doer of makruh [tahrimi] is deprived of that.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from Taftazani’s Al-Talwih upon Sadr al-Shariah's Al-Tawdih, explaining the division of actions into twelve categories based on the logical classification of the obligatee's acts. The core of the passage is the dispute between Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding the definition and placement of makruh tahrimi. The author begins by stating that because there is a disagreement on the definition of makruh tahrimi, the basis for the division of actions also differs. He then presents Imam Muhammad’s method: all acts are either equal (mubah) or one side is preponderant. If the act is preponderant, it is either wajib (if abandonment is prohibited) or mandub (if not). If abandonment is preponderant, the act is either not prohibited (makruh tanzihi) or prohibited. If prohibited, the prohibition is either by definitive proof (haram) or speculative proof (makruh tahrimi). Thus, Imam Muhammad places makruh tahrimi under 'prohibition of the act' (la yajuzu fa‘luhu), distinguishing it from haram only by the strength of the proof. The commentator notes that this is appropriate for the author’s classification in the matn. Next, the passage presents the Shaykhayn's method: they divide acts into equal (mubah) or not. If not equal, the action side being preponderant leads to wajib or mandub. If abandonment is preponderant, if the act is prohibited, it is haram; if not prohibited, it is either closer to permissible (makruh tanzihi) or closer to forbidden (makruh tahrimi). In this view, makruh tahrimi is not a prohibition of the act but is closer to prohibition; the doer is not punished with fire but is blameworthy and may be deprived of intercession. The Shaykhayn thus consider makruh tahrimi as permissible in the sense that it is not strictly forbidden, but it is discouraged and the doer incurs some penalty. The passage then addresses an objection: the commentator’s claim that a person committing makruh tahrimi is deprived of intercession (shafa‘ah) seems inconsistent because major sinners still receive intercession. Several answers are given: (1) deprivation means he cannot intercede for others, (2) it is temporary deprivation, (3) intercession is for major sins; for minor sins, intercession for raising ranks is withheld, or (4) it refers to angelic intercession for the acceptance of prayers. This shows the careful theological and legal reasoning within the Hanafi school regarding the consequences of different categories of acts.

Key Terms
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An action that is prohibited by a speculative proof (dalil zanni); the doer is blameworthy and may be punished, but not with the punishment of haram. According to Imam Muhammad, it is included under 'prohibition of the act' (la yajuzu); according to the Shaykhayn, it is 'close to forbidden' (aqrab ila al-hurmah) but not prohibited.
مکروہ تنزیہی (makruh tanzihi): An action whose abandonment is preponderant but not prohibited; the doer is not punished and the abandoner receives a small reward. It is 'close to permissible' (aqrab ila al-hillah).
واجب (wajib): An action whose performance is demanded definitively, and whose abandonment is prohibited. If abandoned without excuse, the person is punished.
حرام (haram): An action prohibited by a definitive proof (dalil qat‘i); the doer is punished with fire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the legal status of an action that is 'close to forbidden' (aqrab ila al-hurmah) in their classification?
A) It is haram and the doer is punished with fire.
B) It is makruh tahrimi; the doer is not punished with fire but may be deprived of intercession.
C) It is makruh tanzihi; the doer is rewarded for leaving it.
D) It is mubah, neither rewarded nor punished.

Key Takeaway
The internal Hanafi dispute on makruh tahrimi illustrates that a speculative proof (zanni dalil) can lead to different classifications depending on the logical framework adopted—either as a type of prohibition (Imam Muhammad) or as a blameworthy permissible (Shaykhayn).

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
10 min
Two Objections to the Definition of Fiqh and Their Hanafi Responses
Analyzing two objections to the definition of fiqh and their refutations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate objections to definitions of fiqh by applying Hanafi principles on ambiguity and respect for transmitted definitions.

Core Idea
Ambiguity in a definition is not a defect if all possible meanings are true and the addressee may choose.

In this passage, Sadr al-Shariah (al-Tawdih) is defended against two objections to the second definition of fiqh. The first objection claimed that the same problem of 'knowledge of rulings' applies to the first definition. The second objected to the phrase 'mā lahā wa mā alayhā' for having multiple meanings. The Hanafi responses show a sophisticated approach to definitional ambiguity and respect for early authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Recognize that the first definition of fiqh is 'ma'rifat al-nafs mā lahā wa mā alayhā' (knowledge of the soul's rights and duties) and the second is 'al-ilm bi al-ahkam' (knowledge of rulings).
These are standard definitions in Hanafi usul.
2
Understand the first objection
The objection argues that if 'ahkam' means all rulings it is impossible; if specific or unspecified it is unknown. This same objection could apply to the first definition.
This objection originates from Sharh Taftazani.
3
Analyze the responses to the first objection
Three responses are given: (1) The author omitted it out of respect because the definition is from Abu Hanifa. (2) The author intended to object to both definitions equally. (3) The first definition's 'rights and duties' are finite because they pertain to the soul's own actions.
Note the emphasis on respect for imams (adab).
4
Understand the second objection
The phrase 'mā lahā wa mā alayhā' has five possible meanings, causing ambiguity. The objection says such ambiguity is ugly in a definition.
The word 'mā lahā' etc. can mean different things like duties, prohibitions, etc.
5
Apply the Hanafi response on ambiguous words
The response states that if a word admits multiple meanings and all are intended (or can be chosen), it is not defective. Here three out of five meanings are valid and the addressee may choose.
This is consistent with Hanafi usul that does not require univocity.
